Mme. des A. ?You see I can bear it.
N. ?Thanks to us?But for me, as I have had to
prepare all the others?l am quite worn out?Ah!
(falls down on the footstool).
B. ?Oh, heavens, he is ill!
N. ?No, no!
Mme. des A. ? Don?t be uneasy, for as you see, my
children, one does not die of joy!
The End.

The calling of servant, gentlemen, is full of
troubles,
Which pleasure rarely does enliven.
A servant who lets the glasses fall
Almost always for them has got to pay ;
Yes, ponder well, for them we have to pay.

If, by misfortune, their prose I let fall,
